<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A novel circularly polarized (CP) loop antenna design for a UHF band (902-928 MHz) radio frequency identification (RFID) tag is proposed to overcome the polarization mismatch problem between reader antenna and tag antenna. The structure of the proposed tag antenna is a simple square-loop type loaded with an open gap, two feeding strips, and a matching stub. The open gap and two feeding strips were used to achieve good CP radiation. Desirable impedance matching between the tag antenna and RFID chip was attained by tuning the matching stub. Besides achieving satisfactory 3-dB axial-ratio and 10-dB impedance bandwidths of approximately 5.5%, good antenna gain and reading range of more than 2.8 dBic and 16.3 m, respectively, were also demonstrated.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>In Some particular radio frequency identification (RFID) applications such as a car parking management system, a tag antenna with long reading distance is highly required. When a circularly polarized (CP) tag antenna with the same polarized orientation as a CP reader antenna is used, the polarization efficiency will be equivalent to 1, and a 41% (optimum) increment in reading distance can be achieved as compared to a linearly polarized (LP) tag. Hence, the design of a UHF tag antenna with CP radiation is a very important topic of interest in the RFID community. Presently, devising a specific inductive reactance for a passive CP UHF tag antenna is a daunting task for antenna engineers. The RFID chip generally consists of small input resistance and high capacitive reactance. Therefore, the tag antenna must have identical resistance and high inductive reactance (conjugately matched to the chip), so that optimum power transfer can be realized between the chip and tag antenna. In the open literature, very few passive RFID tag antennas with CP radiation have been studied for UHF band <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, two dipole antennas were arranged diagonally for exciting CP radiation. Although this design can achieve compact size and broad CP bandwidth, however, complicated matching circuit was required to connect the two dipoles. Even though the design in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a> has demonstrated desirable gain (6 dBic) and reading distance (8 m), besides exhibiting a narrow CP bandwidth of 15 MHz, this microstrip tag antenna has also exhibited large surface area and thickness of 189×127 mm<sup>2</sup> and 21.6 mm, respectively. Therefore, a low-profile microstrip tag antenna with smaller surface area has been recently studied <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. Nonetheless, the major disadvantages of this design include narrow CP bandwidth (6 MHz) and small gain (−14 dBic in free-space condition). Recently, a number of loop antennas designed with broad CP bandwidth have been investigated <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, but the input impedances for these reported antennas were matched to near 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Notably, the use of loop-type antennas to design passive UHF tag antennas with CP radiation is not reported elsewhere in the open literature.</p><p>In this letter, a novel loop tag antenna with CP radiation is proposed. To conjugately match the loop tag antenna to the tag chip, the technique of loading a matching stub across the tag chip is used. Furthermore, CP radiation can be realized by introducing an open gap and two feeding strips to the square loop. The structure of the proposed loop tag antenna is simple and can be fabricated on thin PET substrate, which leads to the advantages such as low cost and low profile. The design processes of the proposed antenna are explicitly shown, and parametric studies through simulation are carried out. Typical experimental measurement is also conducted and compared to the simulated ones.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Design</h2></div><p>The geometry of the proposed loop tag antenna with surface area of 90×90 mm<sup>2</sup> is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>. The proposed antenna comprises a square loop, two feeding strips, and a matching stub of widths 4, 2, and 3 mm (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="width: 0.423em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.363em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1000.3em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">t</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), respectively. Here, the antenna was constructed by using a copper sheet of thickness 0.15 mm, and Styrofoam with dielectric constant (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-7" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.5em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-9" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">∼</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\sim 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) was placed underneath it [refer to <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>]. An open gap of length 2 mm (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-39" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; </p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>(a) Geometry of the proposed CP RFID loop tag antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-45" role="math" style="width: 2.715em; (b) Photograph of the fabricated tag antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6651751/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The proposed antenna is designed to operate in the RFID UHF band of 902–928 MHz designated for North America. The impedance of the tag chip (Alien IC Higgs) is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-96" role="math" style="width: 6.61em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.949em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.89em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-97"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-98" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">13.5</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-99" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-101" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">111</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-102" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-103" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">13.5 - j 111 ~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 915 MHz, and the minimum threshold power to activate this chip is −14 dBm. Therefore, the input impedance of the proposed antenna must be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-104" role="math" style="width: 6.61em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.949em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.89em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-105"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-106" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">13.5</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-107" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-108" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-109" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">111</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-110" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-111" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">13.5 + j 111 ~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> so that optimum power transfer between the antenna and the tag chip can be achieved. To obtain the desired input impedance, the technique of loading a matching stub across the antenna's feed point is introduced, in which this feed point is the location of the tag chip. By tuning the parameters <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-112" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-114"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-115" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-117"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">L _{x}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-119" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-121"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-122" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-123"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-125" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">L _{y}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-126" role="math" style="width: 0.423em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.363em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1000.3em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-127"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">t</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the matching stub, good conjugate impedance matching can be realized.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Simulated current distributions of proposed CP loop tag antenna at 915 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6651751/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>In this design, the total average length of the square loop is 344 mm, which corresponds roughly to a free-space wavelength (328 mm) of 915 MHz. It should be noted that a one-wavelength square-loop antenna only with an open gap is difficult to induce CP wave <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2">[4]</a>. Therefore, the most important technique in this design is to incorporate two additional feeding strips into the square-loop antenna with an open gap. By properly selecting the lengths (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-129" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-130"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-132" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-134"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">S _{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-136" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.02em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-137"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-138"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-139" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">S _{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the two feeding strips and the location (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-143" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-144"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-145" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the open gap, good CP radiation can be excited. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> shows the simulated current distribution diagrams at four various phases (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-146" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-148" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-149" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">\omega t</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), obtained from the commercial software HFSS. By observing the null current positions (A and B), they are rotated in a clockwise direction as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-150" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1000.9em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-151"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-152" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-153" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-26">\omega t</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is increased from 0° to 270°. Therefore, the proposed loop tag antenna excites left-hand CP (LHCP) radiation.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Results and Discussions</h2></div><p>

top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-202"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-203" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; For the case of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-204" role="math" style="width: 3.366em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.006em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.95em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-205"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-206"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-207" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-208"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-209"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-210" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-211" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-212" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">L _{x} =0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (stub not loaded), the input impedance is too large for conjugate match with the tag chip. However, when the stub is loaded and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-213" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.787em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.55em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-214"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-215"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-216" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-217"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-218"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-219" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-220" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&gt;</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-221" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">16</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-222" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">L _{x} &gt; 16~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm, the resistance level falls to a desirable level that matches the resistance of the tag at approximately 13.5 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-223" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-224"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-225" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Furthermore, at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-226" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.787em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.55em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-227"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-228"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-229" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-230"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-231"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-232" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-233" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">L _{x} =18~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm, the simulated input impedance of the proposed loop tag antenna at 915 MHz is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-236" role="math" style="width: 6.61em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.949em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.89em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-237"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-238" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">13.9</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-239" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-240" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-241" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">110</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-242" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-243" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">13.9 + j 110~ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which yields a result fairly close to a simple conjugate match with the tag chip. Notably, the measured impedance for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-244" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-245"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-246"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-247" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-251" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">L _{x} =18~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm is also plotted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>, and good validation is achieved between the simulation and the measurement. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows the measured and simulated power reflection coefficient of the proposed loop tag antenna with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-254" role="math" style="width: 4.207em; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-255"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-256"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">L _{x} =18~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_3">[1]</a>. The measured impedance bandwidth, determined from −10 dB power reflection coefficient, is 52 MHz (895–947 MHz), and it is enough to cover the RFID UHF band (902–928 MHz).</p><p>

When <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d = 4~</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-376" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-379" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-380" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; In this case, besides achieving an LHCP with desirable AR level of 0.15 dB at 915 MHz, a broad 3-dB AR bandwidth of 50 MHz (5.45%, 892–942 MHz) is also attained, as depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>. Notably, further simulations have also shown that tuning the length <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-396" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-397"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-398" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the open gap can slightly affect the AR level. For brevity, detailed discussion on the parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-399" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-508" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">79</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-509" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">S _{1} + S _{2} =79~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> mm.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6651751/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>In conclusion, this design requires two simple steps to achieve the desired CP radiation at a certain frequency. The first step is to tune the parameters (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-510" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-511"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-512" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">g</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-513" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-514"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-515" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the open gap concurrently, so that optimum AR value can be achieved. The final step is to choose an appropriate length for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-516" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-518"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-519" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-520"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-521"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-522" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">S _{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">S _{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-523" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-524"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-525"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-526" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-527"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-528"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-529" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">S _{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> so that the CP operating frequency can be controlled and shifted to the designated band.</p><p>Since the input impedance of the proposed tag antenna is unable to match to a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-530" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-531"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-532" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> coaxial line, it is difficult to measure either the far-field radiation pattern or gain by making use of a conventional anechoic chamber. Therefore, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> presents only the simulated radiation patterns at 915 MHz for the proposed loop tag antenna. In this figure, typical bidirectional patterns with maximum radiation at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta=0^{\circ}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-533" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-534"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-535" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-536" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-537" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-538" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-539"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-540"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-541" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">∘</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">\theta=0^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 180° are exhibited in the two principal planes (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">x z</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-542" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-543"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-544" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-545" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">x z</script></tex-math></inline-formula>- and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y z</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-546" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-547"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-548" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-549" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">y z</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-planes). As both <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E _{\theta}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-550" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-551"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-552"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-553" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-554"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-555"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-556" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">E _{\theta}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">E _{\phi }</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-557" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-558"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-559"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-560" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-561"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-562"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-563" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϕ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">E _{\phi }</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta=0^{\circ}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-564" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-565"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-566" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-567" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-568" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-569" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-570"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-571"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-572" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">∘</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">\theta=0^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 180° are nearly equal, it shows that the proposed loop antenna has excellent CP radiation. The simulated gain of the proposed loop antenna is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. Slight gain variation between 2.64 and 2.95 dBic is observed within the CP operating bandwidth (892–942 MHz).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Simulated radiation patterns at 915 MHz for the proposed antenna studied in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6651751/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Simulated antenna gain for the proposed antenna studied in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6651751/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Reading Range Measurement</h2></div><p>A prototype loop tag antenna as discussed was fabricated, and an Alien IC Higgs chip was attached to the feed location. To conduct the reading range measurement, an RFID reader module (Favite FS-GM201) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_4">[9]</a> with operating frequency of 902–928 MHz and 30-dBm output power was used, and two RFID reader antennas with different polarizations (LP and CP type) were separately attached to this reader module. Here, the gain of the LP reader antenna (Favite, FS-GA203) is 10 dBi, while the CP reader antenna (Motorola, AN400) is 9 dBic. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>, the maximum reading range measurements were performed by rotating the proposed loop tag antenna along the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-573" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-574"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-575" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϕ</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">\phi</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-direction. The measured results for the two reader antennas are also presented in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6651751/6651751-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Reading range measurements conducted by rotating the proposed CP loop tag antenna in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-576" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-577"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-578" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϕ</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">\phi</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-direction, by separately using the LP and CP reader antennas with gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G _{t} =10~</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-579" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-580"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-581"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.128em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.046em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-582" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.797em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-583"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-584"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-585" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-586" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-587" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">10</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-588" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">G _{t} =10~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dBi and 9 dBic, respectively.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6651751/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>, the reading ranges measured by applying the LP reader antenna are between 12.3 and 12.9 m at all <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-589" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-590"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-591" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϕ</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">\phi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> angles. Therefore, this result further verifies that the proposed loop tag antenna has good CP radiation. As for the CP reader antenna, reading ranges between 15.3 and 16.3 m are obtained at all <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-592" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-593"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-594" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϕ</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">\phi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> angles, which is approximately 3 m longer than the LP type, even though the gain of CP reader antenna (9 dBic) is smaller than the LP type (10 dBi). This is because of polarization matching between the CP reader antenna and the proposed CP loop tag antenna, which can be explained by observing the following Friis equation for calculation of the maximum reading range <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">r _{\max}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-595" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-596"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-597"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-598" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-599"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-600"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-601" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">G _{\rm t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the gain of reader antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P _{\rm r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-718" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-719"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-720"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-721" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-722"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-723"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-724" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">P _{\rm r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the smallest threshold power to activate the tag chip, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">G _{\rm r}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-725" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-726"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-727"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-728" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-729"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-730"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-731" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">G _{\rm r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the gain of tag antenna, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Gamma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-732" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-733"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-734" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Γ</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">\Gamma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the reflection coefficient of the tag antenna, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-735" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-736"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-737" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ρ</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">\rho</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the polarization efficiency. In this letter, since both the reader antenna and the tag antenna are left-handed circularly polarized, thus <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\rho =1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-738" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-739"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-740" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ρ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-741" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-742" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">\rho =1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> shows the comparison between calculated and measured reading range results, and good validation is demonstrated.

<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A CP loop tag antenna for UHF RFID applications has been successfully studied and implemented. The measured impedance bandwidth and CP bandwidth of the proposed loop tag antenna were 52 MHz (895–947 MHz) and 50 MHz (892–942 MHz), respectively. Furthermore, the gain variation within the CP bandwidth was between 2.64 and 2.95 dBic, and the maximum reading range measured by using CP reader antenna was 16.3 m. Therefore, the proposed antenna is an excellent candidate for various RFID applications in the UHF band (902–928 MHz), especially those that may require long reading distance.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

The structure of the proposed tag antenna is a simple square-loop type loaded with an open gap, two feeding strips, and a matching stub. The open gap and two feeding strips were used to achieve good CP radiation. Desirable impedance matching between the tag antenna and RFID chip was attained by tuning the matching stub.
